  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText9189446411020729961" style="display:none"><b><i>#1 Bestseller in Asian-American Literature!<br />Available in paperback, Kindle, and Kindle Unlimited!<br />Winner of the 2019 Independent Press Award </i><br /><br />From the ashes of the Syrian Civil War comes this story of hope, love, and courage... </b><br /><br />After standing for over 7,000 years, Aleppo's ruin came overnight. Separated from his family during the night the rebels attacked the city, 13-year-old Zaid Kadir is lost in the middle of a war zone. Alongside his friends, he is forced to survive the dangers of a civil war he does not even fully understand. <br /><br />Zaid witnesses the destruction of the brutal Syrian Civil War as it grows more deadly by the day and rips his city apart. However, as he braves this destruction, as he desperately tries to survive this catastrophe, he discovers something. Zaid realizes that it is in the darkest hours when humanity's spirit of hope burns brightest.<br /><br /><b>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407763505" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80064765-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529001571p2/80064765.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407763505?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/80064765-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407763505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6837893276379098578"><b> Fantastic novel that touches the heart of the reader </b><br/>I was given an advanced copy of this book by the author in exchange for an honest review. This novel is absolutely heart-wrenching. I was generally aware of what's going on in Syria. However, this story put everything in a different perspective for me. The story focuses on a young teenager, Zaid Kadir, who is separated from his family in Aleppo after it is over run by the rebels. Along with his two best friends, Salman and Fatima, he has to s</span>
  <span id="freeText6837893276379098578" style="display:none"><b> Fantastic novel that touches the heart of the reader </b><br />I was given an advanced copy of this book by the author in exchange for an honest review. This novel is absolutely heart-wrenching. I was generally aware of what's going on in Syria. However, this story put everything in a different perspective for me. The story focuses on a young teenager, Zaid Kadir, who is separated from his family in Aleppo after it is over run by the rebels. Along with his two best friends, Salman and Fatima, he has to survive the horrors of a war that no child should ever have to face. <br /><br />The author does a great job of humanizing Zaid. He's a normal 13-year-old boy no different than any American or European kid. He has dreams for the future. He is experiencing his first true crush (maybe even love). He wants to be accepted by his peers. By the author doing that, I felt like I could relate to Zaid at an entirely different level, and I felt like I was in his place. At times, it felt like I could literally feel the bombs dropping and the shooting as Zaid and his friends have to fight to survive time and time again. <br /><br />Like I've heard the author say, this book isn't about the politics. Instead, it shows the bravery of humanity as we see the people of Aleppo rescuing one another time and time again. We also see humanity at its worst in the form of the rebels, soldiers, and some of Aleppo's citizens who have become lost to the chaos of war. <br /><br />I truly believe this is a book everyone should read! Not only does it give a better understanding of The Syrian Civil War, but it also helps us understand the plight of the people in war torn regions in a way that we might not otherwise get. Thank you to the author for giving me a copy of this book in advance of its publication!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6837893276379098578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408247726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16962299599774718066">We have seen the heartrending images of babies crying on missile-shelled, bullet-riddled streets, heard the furor of debate over desperate people seeking shelter from a war-torn country, but rare is the first-person account from a youthful perspective that gives us a window to feel it all up close. This coming-of-age story (realistic fiction) starts with a 13-year-old Syrian boy running for his life through a battle zone to no safety at all.<br/><br/>The narrative then slams backward, to a place any young</span>
  <span id="freeText16962299599774718066" style="display:none">We have seen the heartrending images of babies crying on missile-shelled, bullet-riddled streets, heard the furor of debate over desperate people seeking shelter from a war-torn country, but rare is the first-person account from a youthful perspective that gives us a window to feel it all up close. This coming-of-age story (realistic fiction) starts with a 13-year-old Syrian boy running for his life through a battle zone to no safety at all.<br /><br />The narrative then slams backward, to a place any young person will recognize: the classroom and a tedious lesson. The teacher is driving home the message of what Assad’s presidency has meant to the people of Syria. Zaid’s classmate Ahmed is one who, echoing his father, presumes Assad is a great man who helped the economy. <br /><br />Readers who have not grown up in dictatorships may find it strange that school lessons include whimsical “leader” stories given on a daily basis. Such propaganda is a reality that children in free societies are spared.<br /><br />Zaid’s life seems normal in the sense that families get up, go to work or school, and come home to eat and sleep, but his 13-year-old neighbor and classmate, Fatima, notices that nine students are absent. <br /><br />The Heart of Aleppo is a courageous and versatile account of young Zaid, who discovers the “heart” of his home city even as it is destroyed. His life moves from some semblance of normality living over his rug merchant father’s shop to learning how to survive with young Fatima and her brother Salman as adults die around them. Zaid comes to question every notion or tradition that structured his life before chaos. Prefabricated ideas of who and what represent safety fall away as government soldiers and rebels fire through civilians to dominate each other. There is no safety.<br /><br />Ammar Habib is a prolific young author who skillfully makes a 7,000-year-old city under onslaught come to life. Readers will feel they are running in the rubble and understand what it must mean when there is no way to stay out of a fight—not when it has engulfed an entire country. I strongly recommend this book not only to young readers but school librarians.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16962299599774718066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2475320188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2475320188" />
    <a title="Mererid Evanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77204618-mererid-evanna"><img alt="Mererid Evanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525594236p2/77204618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2475320188?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mererid Evanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mererid Evanna" href="/user/show/77204618-mererid-evanna">Mererid Evanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2475320188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16506063979859496750">This is way out of my comfort zone: I never read books about war or follow news about it. I've mostly heard about the Syrian Civil War in terms of territories being seized or recovered as if they were pieces on a game board. Zaid, the 13-year-old hero of this story, was similarly protected by his parents from unpleasant and worrying news, so it is all the more shocking for him when he is present at the initial assault on his home town of Aleppo. Within an astonishingly short time, this bright, b</span>
  <span id="freeText16506063979859496750" style="display:none">This is way out of my comfort zone: I never read books about war or follow news about it. I've mostly heard about the Syrian Civil War in terms of territories being seized or recovered as if they were pieces on a game board. Zaid, the 13-year-old hero of this story, was similarly protected by his parents from unpleasant and worrying news, so it is all the more shocking for him when he is present at the initial assault on his home town of Aleppo. Within an astonishingly short time, this bright, bustling, modern city is reduced to a silent, smoking ruin. Zaid and his friends are separated from their families and struggle to return home to them. <br /><br />It becomes clear that neither side in the conflict is even considering the civilians caught in the crossfire. They must rely on themselves. Zaid, the dreamer, finds reserves of strength and courage within himself; gentle Fatima calmly treats knife and gunshot wounds; and her older brother Salman shoulders unaccustomed responsibility. I was impressed with the messages of hope and heroism, and with the restrained treatment of religious faith.<br /><br />I would like to see this book read in schools. It's entirely appropriate for that. It has the excitement of a post-apocalyptic adventure with the sobering knowledge that this destruction actually happened in our lifetime. It powerfully evokes the chaos of war. And also it gives a picture – through flashbacks – of a strong culture and community that our hearts can recognize.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16506063979859496750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2409248571" />
    <a title="Lael Braday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9499723-lael-braday"><img alt="Lael Braday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510071566p2/9499723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2409248571?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lael Braday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lael Braday" href="/user/show/9499723-lael-braday">Lael Braday</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2409248571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15541659415903722118">Thirteen-year-old Zaid and his friends, siblings Fatima and Salman, leave innocence behind when their parents send them away at rumors of rebel attacks. The teenagers discover that nowhere is safe, as they are besieged repeatedly by rebels, and learn that the military cannot be trusted—they are alone. Strangers sacrifice their lives; strangers betray them; strangers ask for help…evoking survival instincts and humanity’s courage in the darkest hours. They are children, separated from their parent</span>
  <span id="freeText15541659415903722118" style="display:none">Thirteen-year-old Zaid and his friends, siblings Fatima and Salman, leave innocence behind when their parents send them away at rumors of rebel attacks. The teenagers discover that nowhere is safe, as they are besieged repeatedly by rebels, and learn that the military cannot be trusted—they are alone. Strangers sacrifice their lives; strangers betray them; strangers ask for help…evoking survival instincts and humanity’s courage in the darkest hours. They are children, separated from their parents, who must fear multiple, murderous factions and their own government, kids who days ago were living normal teenage lives, as any teenager in any country.<br /><br />Habib’s portrayal of Syrian teens on the run from death, as well as their daily lives before the war, was supplemented by his friendships with native Syrians and interviews with Syrian refugees for accuracy. His hope is to bring more awareness to the world of a civil war that has killed hundreds of thousands of civilians who desire only the freedom he enjoys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15541659415903722118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2409261977" />
    <a title="Kimberly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11316615-kimberly"><img alt="Kimberly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213365p2/11316615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2409261977?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly" href="/user/show/11316615-kimberly">Kimberly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2409261977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7437427193427618108"><b>Heart-wrenching, powerful story that portrays heroism and hope under the worst circumstances</b><br/>This is a beautifully written and emotionally charged book that gives its readers a glimpse of the terrible ordeals people in war-torn countries go through. This is not a political tale nor does it take sides in any way. It simply tells the story of an average young man and how his life gets turned upside down when his country and it's government decide war is the only solution to their problems. <br/><br/>This sto</span>
  <span id="freeText7437427193427618108" style="display:none"><b>Heart-wrenching, powerful story that portrays heroism and hope under the worst circumstances</b><br />This is a beautifully written and emotionally charged book that gives its readers a glimpse of the terrible ordeals people in war-torn countries go through. This is not a political tale nor does it take sides in any way. It simply tells the story of an average young man and how his life gets turned upside down when his country and it's government decide war is the only solution to their problems. <br /><br />This story is told in first-person from the perspective of Zaid, a 13-year-old boy that is no different than any 13-year-old boy you may know. He has plans for a future, he has a crush, he has homework. But everything changes around him when his city becomes a war zone that he and all of the other civilians are stuck inside of. <br /><br />Ammar Habib's writing and descriptions are so clear and well-written I could feel the destruction around me and hear the battle as it raged. His characters are so real, my heart hurt for Zaid when he was down and soared for him when he was proving how good people could be. <br /><br />This book truly opened my eyes to things happening in other parts of the world that I'd had no idea about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7437427193427618108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10227907672082151946">A beautiful novel that will stay with me for a long time. Habib managed to write Zaid as a character many people will be able to relate to.   <span id="freeText10227907672082151946" style="display:none">A beautiful novel that will stay with me for a long time. Habib managed to write Zaid as a character many people will be able to relate to. A teenage boy with hopes and dreams of the future, who's innocence is quickly destroyed when the first bombs start to fall. The conflicting emotions Zaid experiences about his brother, his family, the military and life in general are put into words beautifully. Thanks to Habib's writing I was able to really picture Aleppo and the destruction that took place. I would definitely recommend this novel to other people to gain more insight of what is going on in Syria and to see things from a different perspective. Rather than all the news coverage we've all seen before, this novel allows us to understand the humanitarian aspect.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2405864611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11715530180220297901">I was given this ARC by the author in exchange for an honest review: <br/><br/>Wow! That is all I can say. This story absolutely touched my heart. As the premise suggests, this novel follows a young boy, Zaid Kadir, as he is separated from his family in the midst of the Battle of Aleppo. Along with 2 of his friends, he is forced to survive the chaos of war.   <span id="freeText11715530180220297901" style="display:none">I was given this ARC by the author in exchange for an honest review: <br /><br />Wow! That is all I can say. This story absolutely touched my heart. As the premise suggests, this novel follows a young boy, Zaid Kadir, as he is separated from his family in the midst of the Battle of Aleppo. Along with 2 of his friends, he is forced to survive the chaos of war. The book is a balancing act in how it shows the brutality and chaos of war, and helplessness of those caught in the crossfire. <br /><br />The book's theme seems to be the spirit of humanity and that courage is often found in the darkest times. I really appreciated those messages and the way that Habib showed them. I cannot say much without spoiling the story, but I will say that the ending, along with other parts of the novel, had me in tears. <br /><br />What I enjoyed about this novel is that it is not about the politics of war, and it chooses to instead focus on the humanity of war's effects. Habib does a good job of showing how Zaid does not fully grasp the politics of the war, as most children would not. The destruction has a very hollow and abandoned tone, and the characters are very relatable even to those who are not familiar with Syria's culture. It's clear that the author's religious background does help him flesh out the characters. I can honestly say that having read this work has given me a better glimpse into the lives of Syria's war refugees. <br /><br />Thank you to the author for allowing me to read this terrific novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11715530180220297901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2490689984" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2490689984" />
    <a title="Vi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83651425-vi"><img alt="Vi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535099066p2/83651425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2490689984?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vi" href="/user/show/83651425-vi">Vi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2490689984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11253533524906576843">First of all I would like to thank the author as well as Indie Blog Hop for offering me the ARC in exchange for an honest review. This is one of the most emotional reads I've ever come across. I swear. The situations, the killings, everything, it hit me so much that it's just painful and heart-wrenching to read. And the fact that it's based on a real event made it all the more powerful to read because there actually people, so many people, who are affected by this mess. There were so many dreams</span>
  <span id="freeText11253533524906576843" style="display:none">First of all I would like to thank the author as well as Indie Blog Hop for offering me the ARC in exchange for an honest review. This is one of the most emotional reads I've ever come across. I swear. The situations, the killings, everything, it hit me so much that it's just painful and heart-wrenching to read. And the fact that it's based on a real event made it all the more powerful to read because there actually people, so many people, who are affected by this mess. There were so many dreams shattered as well as families lost, and this story showcases that idea to you. This story will follow a thirteen year old Zaid as he and his two other friends try their best to survive and travel back to their home. If there's something that I couldn't love more in this book, it's the main trio—Zaid, Fatima, and Salman. We see a breakthrough of their friendship in the first chapter, the fun and childishness they all have. And though Salman was two years older than the other two, he joins along their banter. And that friendship is just so pure. Then the war came, and you could see it in the story—how they grew up. Salman, being the oldest, has to act stricter and more like a leader towards the two. And they all had to mature—it doesn't matter who throws the rock the longest anymore, it's about survival. And these kids actually pans that idea out to you. The protagonist and his dreams to be a doctor, I love how supportive everyone is over his dream, especially his brother Nabeel (honestly would've wanted more page time with him) I love how every side character in this book all play an important part in Zaid's development. His brother, parents, teacher (don't like his teacher though), Jari, the ___, not just thrown away. "B-but the news... They'll be showing—" "People all over the world will see the reports. It will be on the five 'o clock news as they're eating dinner. They'll see the destruction and maybe some corpses. And do you know what they'll do?" Fatima is silent. "They'll say 'that is horrible'. Then... they change their channel and go right on to their meal." I think what shot this story into new levels was truly the emotion. Like you could immediately tell that the author poured so much tears and laughter into this story because of thay blast of emotion you'll feel. With Jari's death? Heck, that was the first one and I can't even anymore. And the fact wherein Zaid realized that the soldiers were just into making sure that the rebels would die, sacrificing the civilians. And that quote—just KILLED me. Like it hits the fourth wall so much and douses you in reality that you're one of those people, watching and changing the channel and just wow. God-willing. In the past, I always said those words with hope. Tonight, I say them so I don't have to say how I truly feel. And from the look in her eyes, she knows it. Another thing that highlights this desperation is their religion. Like you see in the first parts, they were praying quite religiously throughout the day. And in the middle, they just stopped? I'm glad that they started doing it again but then, you know, that pause. AND THE ENDING. Everything about this book (though I'm still bitter about the ending) is a well-deserved five star rating ❤️ If you're looking for an emotional and powerful read with resonating quotes and characters, this is a book worth taking a look.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11253533524906576843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3361848820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3361848820" />
    <a title="Alex Hudson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116004608-alex-hudson"><img alt="Alex Hudson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590695265p2/116004608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3361848820?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex Hudson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex Hudson" href="/user/show/116004608-alex-hudson">Alex Hudson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3361848820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5928489879353946047"><b>Devastatingly Powerful </b><br/><br/>This is a devastatingly powerful read, an emotional roller coaster, and a story I'll never forget. The author hopes to humanize the tragic stories we see on the news from all the wars across the globe, specifically the Syrian Civil War, and he accomplishes that masterfully! <br/><br/>The protagonist, Zaid Kadir, is a normal pre-teen boy living in Aleppo, Syria. He goes to school, has friends, and is in that "awkward" stage of life. He has a crush, wishes he was as cool as some other</span>
  <span id="freeText5928489879353946047" style="display:none"><b>Devastatingly Powerful </b><br /><br />This is a devastatingly powerful read, an emotional roller coaster, and a story I'll never forget. The author hopes to humanize the tragic stories we see on the news from all the wars across the globe, specifically the Syrian Civil War, and he accomplishes that masterfully! <br /><br />The protagonist, Zaid Kadir, is a normal pre-teen boy living in Aleppo, Syria. He goes to school, has friends, and is in that "awkward" stage of life. He has a crush, wishes he was as cool as some other boys, and looks up to his older brother. But everything changes in one night; everything changes when the City of Aleppo is attacked. Overnight, the peaceful city is turned into a war zone. Zaid is separated from his family, and he must now survive an experience no child should ever go through. <br /><br />The 1st-person narrative style puts you in Zaid's shoes. We feel his confusion, feel his fear, feel every emotion of loneliness that he experiences. But above all else, we see his transformation. The darkest hours often pull out the best of humanity. Zaid's coming-of-age story happens over the course of a few days. We see him go from the fragile boy and into a young adult, one who realizes that his city is not a place. Now, Aleppo's heart is inside its citizens. And Zaid fights to keep that heart alive, to help the people around him. <br /><br />The Heart of Aleppo is a courageous and versatile account of young Zaid, who discovers the “heart” of his home city even as it is destroyed. As the chaos grows worse, Zaid comes to question every notion or tradition that structured his life before chaos. Prefabricated ideas of who and what represent safety fall away as government soldiers and rebels fire through civilians to dominate each other. There is no safety. Not anymore. <br /><br />There is no politics in this story. Just a beautiful tale of the human spirit. Ammar Habib brings this story to life masterfully. I would like to see this book read in schools. It has the excitement of a post-apocalyptic adventure with the sobering knowledge that this destruction actually happened in our lifetime. It evokes the chaos of war and shows how war can wreck entire cities and cultures in the blink of an eye. <br /><br />With the world we live in, we NEED more stories like this! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5928489879353946047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2497136766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2497136766" />
    <a title="Stacy Bosse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16054466-stacy-bosse"><img alt="Stacy Bosse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357249159p2/16054466.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2497136766?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy Bosse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy Bosse" href="/user/show/16054466-stacy-bosse">Stacy Bosse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2497136766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13515524390688065411">The Syrian Civil War is a topic I admittedly don’t know much about, so I learned a few tragic things from reading the book. More importantly than the true events this book describes, I was able to sympathize with the characters, regardless of the cultural differences. I’m an 8th grade teacher, and I plan on purchasing more copies of this and adding them to my classroom library for my students to read. My students can learn a lot about what real courage is by reading this book. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14391913156581010529">Told through the eyes of a 13-year-old boy, <i>The Heart of Aleppo</i> brings alive the horrors of the Syrian Civil War. With their home city of Aleppo turned into a war zone over night in 2012, Zaid and his two closest friends struggle to survive amidst the violence in the streets. <br/>A short novel that packs an intense punch. Powerful, timely and important, infused with a defiant sense of hope in the face of death and destruction. Read it.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15199463491839742591"><b>A Must Read</b><br/><br/>I have to tell you that this has a very difficult review to write for me & to dignify with the respect it deserves. The stories and reality of a war torn Syria and the desperation of their beautiful people fleeing and seeking refuge is something that truly affects me, often, in real life. I have so much compassion for these people and stories I have heard of their journeys have truly impacted my heart.<br/><br/>I had to stop-start this book several times.   <span id="freeText15199463491839742591" style="display:none"><b>A Must Read</b><br /><br />I have to tell you that this has a very difficult review to write for me &amp; to dignify with the respect it deserves. The stories and reality of a war torn Syria and the desperation of their beautiful people fleeing and seeking refuge is something that truly affects me, often, in real life. I have so much compassion for these people and stories I have heard of their journeys have truly impacted my heart.<br /><br />I had to stop-start this book several times. While I could have finished it in a day, my emotions physically wouldn’t allow me to.<br /><br />Through this book is a work of fiction - these stories HAPPEN &amp; are real. These wars are real. There are people every day whose homes have been destroyed in the worst types of brutality, grabbing their children and boarding a rubber boat to cross unforgiving seas just for the TINIEST chance that it could save them; that it could spare them.<br /><br />I believe this book should be read in schools. Be read by everyone. And by anyone who needs a reminder of how lucky they are. This book will stay with me forever &amp; I will pray every day that we never feel the fear or loss that they have.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=adrenaline-rush">adrenaline-rush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=poc-authors">poc-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=middle-school-reads">middle-school-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=arc-reads">arc-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17216487-mc-chanster?shelf=omg-my-heart">omg-my-heart</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3310988770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16509777909025280499">This book was absolutely gut-wrenching, and one that everybody should read. Beautifully written, the author weaves his tale around Zaid, a 13-year-old Syrian boy whose life changes in a single night.<br/><br/>Like many other boys his age, Zaid worries about school, has a crush, and would much rather play with his friends than doing homework. He loves and respects his family, and dreams of being a doctor – if only he could learn to stop daydreaming in class! All was well, until one night, he is roused from</span>
  <span id="freeText16509777909025280499" style="display:none">This book was absolutely gut-wrenching, and one that everybody should read. Beautifully written, the author weaves his tale around Zaid, a 13-year-old Syrian boy whose life changes in a single night.<br /><br />Like many other boys his age, Zaid worries about school, has a crush, and would much rather play with his friends than doing homework. He loves and respects his family, and dreams of being a doctor – if only he could learn to stop daydreaming in class! All was well, until one night, he is roused from sleep and hustled into a car with his two friends, Salman and his sister, Fatima. They are to be sent away because danger was coming soon, and leaving the Aleppo was the only possible way to keep them safe. Unfortunately, they never arrive at their destination and together, they embark on a journey of courage, bravery and determination.<br /><br />I just… LOVE this book. It’s beautiful, emotional, and so well done. The author pulls you right into all of it and I felt like I was with Zaid, Salman and Fatima while they faced rebels and soldiers, bullets and bombs. There is absolutely zero hidden agenda in this book – it’s not about politics, or religion, or swaying the reader to choose a side. Instead, it’s about finding humanity and courage in the face of adversity.<br /><br />I would love to see this in libraries everywhere. It’s extremely relevant and completely approachable for middle school and older. Just an absolutely wonderful book and one hundred percent recommended to everybody.<br /><br />**I got a copy of Heart of Aleppo from the author and Voracious Readers Online for an honest review**</span>

<div id="review_3270576972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3270576972" />
    <a title="Sierra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112882347-sierra"><img alt="Sierra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586408362p2/112882347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3270576972?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sierra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sierra" href="/user/show/112882347-sierra">Sierra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3270576972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12146599169207237256">I really enjoyed reading this book because it demonstrated what life was like in a different part of the world, and it also showed how people support each other like they are family even though they aren't family. We see the power of the human spirit, and the power of hope and courage. Though it's a coming-of-age story and a hero's journey for Zaid Kadir, it is so much more. In today's world, this is the sort of book that must be read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15486307941452519301">The book deals with an important topic which has been in the news very frequently. What has not been in the news were the people who suffered during that time. This book is fictitious - the plot is fictitious but the people and their stories are real.<br/><br/>The story is a story about human spirit and going on in life even though the chances and hopes may amount to nothing. The writing made me connect with the characters more and I feel that it made me visualize the story even better. The author paints </span>
  <span id="freeText15486307941452519301" style="display:none">The book deals with an important topic which has been in the news very frequently. What has not been in the news were the people who suffered during that time. This book is fictitious - the plot is fictitious but the people and their stories are real.<br /><br />The story is a story about human spirit and going on in life even though the chances and hopes may amount to nothing. The writing made me connect with the characters more and I feel that it made me visualize the story even better. The author paints a good picture of the Aleppo - before and after war in the minds of the readers, which helps to enjoy and understand the story more.<br /><br />Hope and sacrifice are main themes as they relate to freedom. Your life is deemed of no value if you don't have your rights and freedom. All these rights and freedom are taken away during war and what one has to face is beyond imaginable! The author also focuses on the fact that how children are the ones most affected during the crisis. They are robbed off their childhood and happiness, most of them lose their parents and some even their lives.<br /><br />I feel this book is on an important topic everyone should read about to understand the pain and suffering one goes through during a war crisis.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15486307941452519301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3037774491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3037774491" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51980744-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453835536p2/51980744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3037774491?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/51980744-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037774491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11851595097629550588">As with most war stories, the story told in The Heart of Aleppo is heartbreaking. Ammar Habib does a great job with the voice of a 13-year-old enduring the destruction of Aleppo during the Syrian Civil War. One of the things that impressed me was Habib’s ability to tell the story without including the politics of the war. It is truly a story of the spirit of humanity in difficult circumstances.<br/>While it is a very sad story and hard to read in many ways, I was compelled to keep reading to find out</span>
  <span id="freeText11851595097629550588" style="display:none">As with most war stories, the story told in The Heart of Aleppo is heartbreaking. Ammar Habib does a great job with the voice of a 13-year-old enduring the destruction of Aleppo during the Syrian Civil War. One of the things that impressed me was Habib’s ability to tell the story without including the politics of the war. It is truly a story of the spirit of humanity in difficult circumstances.<br />While it is a very sad story and hard to read in many ways, I was compelled to keep reading to find out what was coming next. Main character Zaid shows growth and maturity beyond that of most of the 13-year-olds I know - but then none of the 13-year-olds I know have had to face their home town being destroyed by war. <br />I think The Heart of Aleppo would be a great addition to a current events unit or Middle East study. This young adult novel should be read by today’s teens to help them better understand the world we live in as well as a glimpse of Muslim beliefs. <br />I would not hesitate to add The Heart of Aleppo to my k-12 Christian school library. <br />I want to thank Prism Book Tours for the complimentary copy of The Heart of Aleppo. This is my honest review. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11851595097629550588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2855622589" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2855622589" />
    <a title="Bruce K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98452702-bruce-k"><img alt="Bruce K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560354275p2/98452702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2855622589?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce K." href="/user/show/98452702-bruce-k">Bruce K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2855622589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5154978032012437803">I could not turn away from this story. The way in which the author weaves together the intimate thoughts of the characters with the outward atrocities of a war torn country is astounding. As you enter into the journey of the beautiful and fiercely brave souls, your heart is overwhelmed with empathy and emotion. "The Heartof Aleppo" is a phenomenal story. A tale that should be discussed and shared. Five well deserved, if not more, stars. Well done, Ammar Habib.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2447273256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447273256" />
    <a title="Sarah Rayner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18005176-sarah-rayner"><img alt="Sarah Rayner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362323672p2/18005176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447273256?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Rayner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Rayner" href="/user/show/18005176-sarah-rayner">Sarah Rayner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447273256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5601018258951976408">Moving tale of how war effects children! I have seen the war reported on the news, but this book really brings it home how it has affected families on a day to day basis. There is no mention of the politics of the war, just the story of group of children. Highly recommend read!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2635008736409064892"><b>5 stars</b><br/><br/>Although not an easy read, I was taken in by the beautiful prose and message of The Heart of Aleppo. Don't let the troubling subject matter turn you away from this excellent book. Well done, touching, inspiring and maddening at the reality of the story. A truly gorgeous book. I cried throughout at the trauma and connection these characters experienc</span>
  <span id="freeText2635008736409064892" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b><br /><br />Although not an easy read, I was taken in by the beautiful prose and message of The Heart of Aleppo. Don't let the troubling subject matter turn you away from this excellent book. I finished reading it several weeks ago and expect to reflect on it for a long time.<br /><br />This is a devastating story of loss and living with hope. Well done, touching, inspiring and maddening at the reality of the story. A truly gorgeous book. I cried throughout at the trauma and connection these characters experienced. I'll never forget this story. <br /></span>

<div id="review_3283419168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3283419168" />
    <a title="Isabella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/113345845-isabella"><img alt="Isabella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587010291p2/113345845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3283419168?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabella" href="/user/show/113345845-isabella">Isabella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3283419168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15960212040297601785">From the moment I started reading this novel, I knew it would be challenging for me to close it after I finished reading. The Syrian War is something I knew about, but this novel brings it to life. This book may be merely fiction, but it makes everything seem so real that I would never be able to tell the difference if I didn't know that it was fictional. It delivers an eerie theme of how a single event can lead to many other events, eventually collapsing the lives of ordinary people. I am so gl</span>
  <span id="freeText15960212040297601785" style="display:none">From the moment I started reading this novel, I knew it would be challenging for me to close it after I finished reading. The Syrian War is something I knew about, but this novel brings it to life. This book may be merely fiction, but it makes everything seem so real that I would never be able to tell the difference if I didn't know that it was fictional. It delivers an eerie theme of how a single event can lead to many other events, eventually collapsing the lives of ordinary people. I am so glad I stumbled upon this novel. It's the most well-written realistic fiction novel I have ever read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15960212040297601785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K5xwiVIO+fbyUxbW+QlR+T7lk243PhA/5W8H3221p3amcwiAsFdaKHwGN+p3ZVEBL9mZXTCwLhQnqaq8uINCuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Beloved and hated, venerated and reviled, Andrew Jackson was an orphan who fought his way to the pinnacle of power, bending the nation to his will in the cause of democracy. Jackson\'s election in 1828 ushered in a new and lasting era in which the people, not distant elites, were the guiding force in American politics. Democracy made its stand in the Jackson years, and he gave voice to the hopes and the fears of a restless, changing nation facing challenging times at home and threats abroad. To tell the saga of Jackson\'s presidency, acclaimed author Jon Meacham goes inside the Jackson White House. Drawing on newly discovered family letters and papers, he details the human drama-the family, the women, and the inner circle of advisers- that shaped Jackson\'s private world through years of storm and victory.\n\nOne of our most significant yet dimly recalled presidents, Jackson was a battle-hardened warrior, the founder of the Democratic Party, and the architect of the presidency as we know it. His story is one of violence, sex, courage, and tragedy. With his powerful persona, his evident bravery, and his mystical connection to the people, Jackson moved the White House from the periphery of government to the center of national action, articulating a vision of change that challenged entrenched interests to heed the popular will- or face his formidable wrath. The greatest of the presidents who have followed Jackson in the White House-from Lincoln to Theodore Roosevelt to FDR to Truman-have found inspiration in his example, and virtue in his vision.\n\nJackson was the most contradictory of men. The architect of the removal of Indians from their native lands, he was warmly sentimental and risked everything to give more power to ordinary citizens. He was, in short, a lot like his country: alternately kind and vicious, brilliant and blind; and a man who fought a lifelong war to keep the republic safe-no matter what it took.<\/span>\n  <a His exhilarating narrative will captivate readers, providing welcome confirmation that this nation can produce presidents who bring leadership to great issues, hold to their purpose, and shape the destinies of nations. \n\nPresident McKinley\'s assassination brought the 43-year-old TR a challenging presidency, one to which Morris is a clearsighted guide. At home, TR had to persuade Congress to curb competition-stifling corporate trusts, monopolistic transcontinental railroads, and unhygienic food industries that saw consumers as sheep. He also faced labor and racial strife. Abroad, the American presence in Cuba and the Philippines brought criticism, the Russo-Japanese conflict threatened major power shifts in the Far East and Europe, and a politically and financially fraught decision on the Central American canal route - Panama or Nicaragua? - had to be made. TR rose to every challenge. Despite the demands of family and social life, he read, wrote, and traveled extensively. Not least, TR put national parks and conservation of natural resources on the legislative agenda.\n\nAll TR\'s notable contemporaries - including historian Henry Adams, naturalists John Burroughs and John Muir, robber barons E. H. Harriman and James J. Hill, poet Oliver Wendell Holmes, financier J. P. Morgan, fellow politician William Howard Taft, civil rights leader Booker T. Washington, and novelist Owen Wister - appear onstage, their clear voices projecting the excitement of the day.\n\nMorris is blessed with the imagination and skills to write gripping popular history. He doesn\'t dilute but illuminates events in presenting an account that immediately sparks interest and captures the mind. Readers will note that American interventionism abroad (today\'s major issue) was much debated during TR\'s presidency, when major interventional imperatives challenged the new superpower\'s tradition of relative restraint in foreign affairs.\n\nTheodore Rex is the long-awaited second volume of the TR saga. Morris delivered the first volume, \n  The Rise of Theodore Roosevelt\n, in 1979. It won a Pulitzer Prize; Theodore Rex is a solid bet for another. \n(Peter Skinner)<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"231907338696186274\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return
